## 1. Who is Steve Yegge?

### Professional Background

Steve Yegge is a 40-year software development veteran with a career that provides unique credibility for building Gas Town:

| Company | Role | Relevance |
|---------|------|-----------|
| **Amazon** | Early employee | Built internal tools at scale |
| **Google** | Senior Engineer | Famous for "Stevey's Blog Rants," internal platforms |
| **Sourcegraph** | Senior role | Code intelligence, developer tooling |
| **Current** | Full-time AI development advocate | Building the future of agent-assisted dev |

### Why His Opinion Matters

- **~1 million lines vibe-coded in 2025** - Not theory, practice
- **Built Beads (225K lines of Go)** - Proof of concept at scale
- **Built Gas Town using Gas Town** - Recursive validation
- **Transparent about limitations** - Warns about chaos, costs, maturity
- **Decades of platform engineering** - Knows what scales and what breaks

### Public Presence

- **Twitter/X:** @steve_yegge (primary announcements)
- **Medium:** steve-yegge.medium.com (deep philosophical pieces)
- **GitHub:** github.com/steveyegge (Gas Town, Beads, MCP Agent Mail)
- **Podcasts:** Changelog, O'Reilly Radar

### The "Vibe Coding" Pioneer

Steve didn't just adopt AI-assisted development - he pioneered "vibe coding" as a philosophy:

> "Work becomes fluid, an uncountable that you sling around freely, like slopping shiny fish into wooden barrels at the docks."

**Vibe coding principles:**
- Describe what you want (the "vibe")
- AI generates the code
- You never read the code directly
- Judge by outcomes, not implementation
- Accept some bugs, focus on throughput

---

## 2. The Gas Town Mental Model

### The Core Insight

> "Claude Code is the world's biggest fuckin' ant. Everyone is focused on making their ant run longer... when nature prefers colonies."

This is the fundamental shift Gas Town represents:

```
TRADITIONAL APPROACH                 GAS TOWN APPROACH
‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ                ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ

     One Big Ant                     Ant Colony
         |                               |
    Make it                        Build the
    run longer                     factory
         |                               |
    Context window               Multiple workers
    limits everything            share the load
         |                               |
    You are the                  You are the
    programmer                   Product Manager
```

### The Factory Metaphor

Gas Town isn't an agent - it's a **factory for agents**:

| Traditional Dev | Gas Town |
|-----------------|----------|
| You write code | You file features |
| You debug | Agents debug |
| You're the implementer | You're the PM |
| Single context window | Many workers, shared memory |
| Session ends, context lost | Workers persist, memory survives |

### The "Idea Compiler"

> "Gas Town is an Idea Compiler. You just make up features, design them, file the implementation plans, and sling work around to your polecats and crew."

**Input:** Your ideas and feature requests
**Output:** Working code, shipped products

You're not writing code anymore. You're managing a factory.

### Why "Gas Town"?

The Mad Max: Fury Road reference isn't accidental:

- **Post-apocalyptic resourcefulness** - Work with chaos, not against it
- **Clear role hierarchy** - Mayor, Deacon, Dogs, Workers
- **Survival-focused** - Throughput over perfection
- **Community-built** - Everyone contributes to the economy

---

## 3. The 8 Roles Architecture

### Hierarchy Overview

```
‚ïî‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïó

‚ïë  ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò  ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò  ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò               ‚ïë
‚ïë          ‚îÇ                    ‚îÇ                    ‚îÇ                       ‚ïë

‚ïë                               ‚îÇ                                            ‚ïë

‚ïë  RIG LEVEL (Per-Project - Multiple instances)                              ‚ïë

```

### Role Deep Dives

#### 1. Mayor (Town-Level Coordination)

**Function:** Chief coordinator - your concierge and chief-of-staff

**Responsibilities:**
- Receives high-level directives from Overseer
- Routes work to appropriate rigs
- Manages cross-rig coordination
- Handles town-level decisions
- Primary AI coordinator for the entire town

**Commands:**
```bash
gt mayor up        # Start mayor
gt mayor status    # Check mayor state
gt mayor down      # Stop mayor
```

**Model recommendation:** Opus 4.5 (complex coordination requires top-tier reasoning)

---

#### 2. Deacon (Monitoring/Handshakes)

**Function:** Health monitoring and agent coordination

**Responsibilities:**
- Monitors agent health across the town
- Handles agent-to-agent handshakes
- Reports anomalies to Mayor
- Tracks work progress
- Manages handoff protocols and worker recycling

**Commands:**
```bash
gt deacon up       # Start deacon
gt deacon status   # View monitoring state
```

**Model recommendation:** Haiku (simple health checks don't need heavy reasoning)

---

#### 3. Dogs (Quality Gates/Watchdogs)

**Function:** Quality assurance and safety gates - town-level grunts

**Responsibilities:**
- Reviews work before acceptance
- Enforces quality standards
- Guards against regressions
- Can reject/rollback work
- Stale branch cleanup

**Commands:**
```bash
gt dogs up         # Start dogs
gt dogs bark       # Trigger quality check
```

**Model recommendation:** Sonnet (quality review requires reasoning, not Opus-level)

---

#### 4. Refinery (Task Decomposition)

**Function:** Breaks down large tasks into agent-sized work

**Responsibilities:**
- Receives feature requests from Mayor
- Decomposes into smaller, atomic tasks
- Assigns to Polecats or Crew
- Tracks decomposition progress
- Manages the merge queue with sequential rebasing

**Commands:**
```bash
gt refinery up <rig>           # Start refinery for rig
gt refinery decompose <task>   # Manually trigger decomposition
```

**Model recommendation:** Opus 4.5 (task decomposition is architecturally complex)

---

#### 5. Polecat (Named Persistent Workers)

**Function:** Named, persistent agent workers with specializations

**Responsibilities:**
- Execute assigned tasks
- Maintain context across sessions
- Specialize in rig-specific knowledge
- Report completion to Refinery
- Ephemeral but can be persistent workspaces

**Commands:**
```bash
gt polecat up <rig> alice      # Start polecat named "alice"
gt polecat up <rig> bob        # Start polecat named "bob"
gt polecat list <rig>          # List polecats for rig
gt polecat assign alice <task> # Assign task to alice
```

**Naming convention:** Human names (alice, bob, carol) help with mental model

**Model recommendation:** Sonnet (implementation work, main workhorse)

---

#### 6. Witness (Per-Rig Observer)

**Function:** Observes and records rig activity - watches over polecats

**Responsibilities:**
- Watches all work in assigned rig
- Records history and context
- Provides state to new workers
- Reports anomalies to Deacon
- Unsticks drifting agents

**Commands:**
```bash
gt witness up <rig>    # Start witness for rig
gt witness report      # Get current state report
```

**Model recommendation:** Haiku (observation and logging don't need heavy reasoning)

---

#### 7. Crew (Ephemeral Workers)

**Function:** Short-lived, task-specific burst workers

**Responsibilities:**
- Execute single tasks
- No persistent state
- Cheap and disposable
- Used for parallel bursts
- Spawn, complete, disappear

**Commands:**
```bash
gt crew spawn <rig> --task "fix this bug"
gt crew count <rig>    # Count active crew
gt crew purge <rig>    # Kill all crew
```

**Model recommendation:** Haiku (simple, isolated tasks)

---

#### 8. Overseer (Human Boss - YOU)

**Function:** Product Manager and decision maker

**Responsibilities:**
- Define features and priorities
- Review inbox decisions
- Approve major changes
- Provide human judgment
- Has identity in the system with own inbox

**Interface:**
- Human inbox for decisions
- tmux panes for observation
- `gt` CLI for commands
- Can send and receive town mail

> "That's you, Human. As the Overseer, you have an identity in the system, and your own inbox, and you can send and receive town mail."

---

### Role Communication Flow

```
[Overseer: YOU]
     ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ "Build user authentication"
     ‚ñº
[Mayor] ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê

     ‚îÇ routes to rig                            ‚îÇ status reports

     ‚îÇ                           ‚îÇ              ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ decomposes into:          ‚îÇ progress     ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ - task 1: DB schema       ‚îÇ              ‚îÇ

     ‚îÇ
     ‚îÇ if passes
     ‚ñº
[Complete]
```

---

## 4. Beads: The Memory System

### The "50 First Dates" Problem

> "Agents suffer from '50 First Dates' syndrome - they wake up with no memory of yesterday."

Every new Claude session starts fresh. This is the fundamental problem Beads solves.

### Why Markdown Plans Fail at Scale

| Problem | Consequence |
|---------|-------------|
| Not queryable | Agents must parse dozens of files to reconstruct work graph |
| No dependency tracking | Agents can't compute which tasks are unblocked |
| Conflict-prone | Multiple agents editing same files |
| Implicit task stacks | "Intelligent wandering" without clear direction |

### What Beads Does

**Beads** (github.com/steveyegge/beads) is a ~225K line Go project providing:

- **Git-backed storage:** All state persisted in git
- **Universal context:** Shared context across all agents
- **Memory management:** Agents can read/write context
- **Hash-based IDs:** (e.g., `bd-a1b2`) prevent merge conflicts
- **Dependency tracking:** Explicit links between tasks
- **Memory decay:** Compaction summarizes old closed tasks

### Beads Architecture

```
‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
‚îÇ                       GAS TOWN                               ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê  ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê  ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îÇ   Mayor    ‚îÇ  ‚îÇ   Polecat  ‚îÇ  ‚îÇ    Crew    ‚îÇ             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¨‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò  ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¨‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò  ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¨‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ        ‚îÇ                ‚îÇ               ‚îÇ                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ        ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îº‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                         ‚îÇ                                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                   ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚ñº‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                   ‚îÇ   BEADS   ‚îÇ                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                   ‚îÇ Data Plane‚îÇ                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¨‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò                             ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                         ‚îÇ                                    ‚îÇ
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îº‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò

                   ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
                   ‚îÇ    Git      ‚îÇ
                   ‚îÇ Repository  ‚îÇ
                   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
```

### Key Beads Commands

```bash
bd ready           # List tasks with zero blockers (what can be done NOW)
bd create "Title"  # Create new task
bd dep add X Y     # X is blocked by Y
bd show <id>       # Full task state and history
```

### Memory Model

```
‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
‚îÇ                    BEADS MEMORY MODEL                        ‚îÇ
‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
‚îÇ                                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  LAYER 1: Hot Context (RAM-cached)                          ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Current task state                                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Last N interactions                                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Active file references                                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  LAYER 2: Warm Context (SQLite + Git index)                 ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Recent commit history                                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Cross-agent message log                                ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Rig state snapshots                                    ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  LAYER 3: Cold Context (Git history)                        ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Full project history                                   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Previous run outcomes                                  ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Archived decisions                                     ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                              ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  RETRIEVAL: Hot ‚Üí Warm ‚Üí Cold (only query cold if needed)   ‚îÇ
‚îÇ                                                              ‚îÇ
‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
```

### Why Git as Database?

> "Git as database provides durable, diffable, auditable storage with zero infrastructure."

- **Survives crashes:** Everything is committed
- **Audit trail:** Full history of all agent actions
- **Recovery:** Roll back to any point in time
- **Sharing:** Multiple agents share the same store
- **No heavyweight message bus required**

---

## 5. The 6 Waves of AI

Steve frames the evolution of AI-assisted development as six overlapping waves:

| Wave | Era | Description | Productivity |
|------|-----|-------------|--------------|
| 1 | Pre-2022 | Traditional manual coding | Baseline |
| 2 | 2023 | Completions-based (Copilot-style) | ~2x |
| 3 | 2024 | Chat-based (CHOP) | ~5x |
| 4 | 2025 H1 | Coding agents (Claude Code, Amp, Codex) | ~10x |
| 5 | 2025 H2 | Agent clusters (multi-agent parallel) | ~25x |
| **6** | **2026+** | **Agent fleets (AI supervisors managing swarms)** | **~50x+** |

**Gas Town is Wave 6 infrastructure.**

### The 8 Stages of Dev Evolution

| Stage | Description |
|-------|-------------|
| 1 | Zero/near-zero AI |
| 2 | Agent in IDE, permissions on |
| 3 | Agent in IDE, YOLO mode |
| 4 | Agent fills screen, code is just diffs |
| 5 | CLI single agent, YOLO |
| 6 | CLI multi-agent (3-5 parallel) |
| 7 | 10+ agents, hand-managed |
| **8** | **Building your own orchestrator** |

**Critical Warning:**
> "If you're not at Stage 7, you'll get your face ripped off by superintelligent chimpanzees."

Gas Town is for Stage 7+ developers. If you're not there yet, go back to Ralph loops.

---

## 6. Core Principles

### GUPP: The Universal Propulsion Principle

> "If there is work on your hook, YOU MUST RUN IT."

This solves the fundamental problem that "Claude Code ends":

- Work is "slung" to agent hooks (persistent git worktrees)
- When an agent starts, it checks its hook
- If work exists, execution is immediate - no confirmation, no waiting
- Work survives crashes and restarts

**The Gupp Nudge:** Claude Code is "so miserably polite" that GUPP doesn't always work. Gas Town implements a "Gupp Nudge" - agents get a startup poke with `gt nudge` roughly 30-60 seconds after starting.

---

### Zero Framework Cognition

> "Claude makes all decisions. The orchestrator executes."

**Key design principle:** All decisions delegated to AI. No heuristics, regex, or parsing in the orchestrator. The framework provides infrastructure, not intelligence.

---

### Agents as Cattle, Not Pets

This is Kubernetes thinking applied to agents:

- Individual sessions are ephemeral
- The work graph is persistent
- The agent is not the session
- The agent is a Bead (identity with a global address)

---

### Nondeterministic Idempotence

Workflows can be interrupted and resumed at any time:

- Path is fully nondeterministic - different runs take different routes
- Workflow eventually finishes as long as you keep throwing agents at it
- Agents may make mistakes but self-correct because acceptance criteria are well-specified
- The system is resilient to individual component failures

---

### Token Spend as Health Metric

> "Token spend per developer per unit time is the new health metric that best represents how well your company is doing with AI."

**The math:**
- Agent cost: ~$10-12 per operating hour
- Recommended daily developer LLM budget: $100-300
- Yegge's personal spend: ~$300/day, ~$80,000/year
- Gas Town workshops generate 12,000 LOC/day per developer

---

### Talk to the Plan, Not the Agent

Because agents have limited context windows and experience "amnesia":

- Maintain persistent, readable plans in files
- Both you and agents reference these plans
- "Land the Plane" pattern: At session end, clean up git, update issues, spit out prompt for next session

---

## 7. Implementation Guide

### Prerequisites Checklist

Before installing Gas Town, verify:

- [ ] **Go 1.21+** installed (`go version`)
- [ ] **tmux** installed and proficient (`tmux -V`)
- [ ] **Multiple Claude accounts** for parallel agents
- [ ] **Stage 7+ experience** (100+ hours multi-agent)
- [ ] **High chaos tolerance** (some bugs, some lost work)
- [ ] **Budget:** $50-200/day

### Installation

```bash
# Step 1: Install Gas Town
go install github.com/steveyegge/gastown/cmd/gt@latest

# Step 2: Verify installation
gt version

# Step 3: Initialize your town (creates ~/.gt)
gt init
```

**Checkpoint:** You should see `Town initialized at ~/.gt`

### Adding Your First Rig

```bash
# Add a project rig
gt rig add /path/to/your/project

# Verify
gt rig list
```

**Checkpoint:** Your project should appear in the rig list

### Starting the Core Roles

Recommended startup sequence:

```bash
# 1. Start town-level roles first
gt mayor up
gt deacon up
gt dogs up

# 2. Start rig-level infrastructure
gt witness up my-project
gt refinery up my-project

# 3. Start named workers
gt polecat up my-project alice
gt polecat up my-project bob
gt polecat up my-project carol
```

**Checkpoint:** `gt status` should show all roles running

### tmux Workflow

Gas Town is tmux-native. Understand this structure:

```
‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê

‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  Mayor       ‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  Polecat     ‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  Polecat    ‚îÇ ‚îÇ
‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  Agent       ‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  Alice       ‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  Bob        ‚îÇ ‚îÇ

```

### Startup Script

Save this as `gastown-start.sh`:

```bash
#!/bin/bash
SESSION="gastown"

# Kill existing session if requested
if [ "$1" = "--fresh" ]; then
  tmux kill-session -t $SESSION 2>/dev/null
fi

# Create session
tmux new-session -d -s $SESSION -n 'overview'

# Infrastructure windows
tmux new-window -t $SESSION -n 'mayor'
tmux new-window -t $SESSION -n 'infra'
tmux split-window -h -t $SESSION:infra

# Per-rig windows
for RIG in project1 project2; do
  tmux new-window -t $SESSION -n "rig-$RIG"
  tmux split-window -h -t "rig-$RIG"
done

# Polecat windows
for POLECAT in alice bob carol; do
  tmux new-window -t $SESSION -n "$POLECAT"
done

# Inbox window
tmux new-window -t $SESSION -n 'inbox'

# Start roles
tmux send-keys -t $SESSION:mayor 'gt mayor up' C-m
tmux send-keys -t $SESSION:infra.0 'gt deacon up' C-m
tmux send-keys -t $SESSION:infra.1 'gt dogs up' C-m
tmux send-keys -t $SESSION:rig-project1.0 'gt witness up project1' C-m
tmux send-keys -t $SESSION:rig-project1.1 'gt refinery up project1' C-m
tmux send-keys -t $SESSION:alice 'gt polecat up project1 alice' C-m
tmux send-keys -t $SESSION:bob 'gt polecat up project1 bob' C-m
tmux send-keys -t $SESSION:inbox 'watch -n 5 gt inbox' C-m

# Attach
tmux select-window -t $SESSION:overview
tmux attach -t $SESSION
```

### Typical Daily Workflow

```bash
# Morning: Start town
./gastown-start.sh

# Review overnight status
gt status
gt inbox

# File new feature
gt inbox send my-project "Build user authentication"

# Refinery decomposes, assigns to polecats
# You review pending decisions
gt inbox respond 5 --approve
gt inbox respond 7 --approve

# Monitor throughout day (switch tmux windows)
# Dogs run quality checks automatically

# Evening: Review completed work
gt inbox review
gt approve 12 15 18  # Approve completed items

# End of day (polecats persist, crew killed)
gt crew purge my-project
```

---

## 8. Checkpoints and Verification

### Post-Installation Checkpoints

| Step | Command | Expected Output |
|------|---------|-----------------|
| Go installed | `go version` | `go version go1.21+` |
| gt installed | `gt version` | Version number |
| Town initialized | `gt status` | Shows town state |
| Rig added | `gt rig list` | Shows your project |
| Mayor running | `gt mayor status` | `running` |

### Health Checks

```bash
# Check all role status
gt status

# Check specific rig
gt rig status my-project

# View agent health
gt deacon report
```

**Healthy state indicators:**
- All roles show `running`
- Deacon reports no anomalies
- Inbox has reasonable pending items (not 100+)
- Polecats are progressing on tasks

### Quality Verification

```bash
# Trigger Dogs quality check
gt dogs bark

# Review what passed/failed
gt dogs report
```

---

## 9. Troubleshooting

### Common Failures and Recovery

#### 1. Context Collapse

**Symptom:** Agents stop making sense, circular reasoning

**Cause:** Beads state corruption or no auto-compact

**Recovery:**
```bash
gt town reset --soft   # Keep config, clear state
gt beads sync --force  # Force context resync
```

---

#### 2. Race Conditions / Merge Conflicts

**Symptom:** Conflicting commits, overwritten work

**Cause:** Multiple Polecats editing same files

**Recovery:**
- Use git worktrees for file isolation
- Implement file ownership rules
- Use the Refinery's merge queue

```bash
# Check for conflicts
git status

# If conflicts exist
gt refinery resolve my-project
```

---

#### 3. Runaway Crew

**Symptom:** Cost spike, dozens of Crew spawned unexpectedly

**Cause:** Refinery misconfiguration or task explosion

**Recovery:**
```bash
# Kill all crew immediately
gt crew purge --all

# Set limits
gt config set crew.max_per_rig 5
gt config set crew.idle_timeout 15
```

---

#### 4. Mayor Deadlock

**Symptom:** No work getting assigned, town seems stuck

**Cause:** Mayor waiting for human decision on something

**Recovery:**
```bash
# Check inbox
gt inbox

# Approve/reject pending items
gt inbox respond <id> --approve
gt inbox respond <id> --reject
```

---

#### 5. Beads Desync

**Symptom:** Agents have stale context, working on old state

**Cause:** Git conflicts in Beads repo

**Recovery:**
```bash
# Force sync
gt beads sync --force

# If that fails, reset Beads
gt beads reset
```

---

#### 6. Agent Won't Start

**Symptom:** `gt polecat up` returns error

**Cause:** Claude account issue, rate limiting, or config problem

**Recovery:**
```bash
# Check config
gt config list

# Try different account
gt config set polecat.alice.account secondary

# Check Claude status
claude --version
```

---

### Recovery Command Reference

```bash
# Soft reset (keep config)
gt town reset --soft

# Hard reset (full reinstall)
gt town reset --hard

# Kill all agents
gt town down

# Restart specific role
gt polecat down my-project alice
gt polecat up my-project alice

# Force Beads sync
gt beads sync --force

# Clear inbox backlog
gt inbox clear --all

# Emergency cost stop
gt pause --all  # Pause all work
gt resume --all # Resume when ready
```

---

## 10. When to Use Gas Town

### Use Gas Town When:

- You're at Stage 7+ (10+ agents, comfortable with chaos)
- Budget is not a concern ($50-200/day)
- You want **team-scale output** as a solo developer
- You have clear product vision but need implementation velocity
- You're comfortable with imperfection (some bugs fixed 2-3 times)
- You have tmux proficiency
- You understand the PM ‚Üí engineering team mental model

### Don't Use Gas Town When:

- You're below Stage 6 on the dev evolution scale
- Budget is constrained
- You need polish and stability
- You need predictable, controlled outcomes
- You're not comfortable with chaos
- The project is simple enough for Ralph loops
- You haven't mastered Levels 0-6 on the complexity ladder

### Decision Matrix


## 11. Quotes and Key Statements

### On the Core Philosophy

> "Claude Code is the world's biggest fuckin' ant. Everyone is focused on making their ant run longer... when nature prefers colonies."

> "Gas Town is an Idea Compiler. You just make up features, design them, file the implementation plans, and sling work around to your polecats and crew."

> "Work becomes fluid, an uncountable that you sling around freely, like slopping shiny fish into wooden barrels at the docks."

### On Expectations

> "Some bugs fixed 2-3 times. Some fixes get lost. Focus: THROUGHPUT, not perfection."

> "You're not a programmer anymore. You're the head chef of a kitchen with AI robotic sous chefs."

### On Prerequisites

> "If you're not at Stage 7, you'll get your face ripped off by superintelligent chimpanzees."

> "If you have any doubt whatsoever, then you can't use it."

### On Maturity

> "Code is 3 weeks old - smuggled 400 miles upriver in my ass."

> "100% vibe-coded - I have never looked at the code myself."

### On Cost

> "If you care about costs, don't use this."

> "Expensive as hell - multiple Claude accounts needed."

### On Language Choice

> "Go is just... good. It's boring. You can always understand it!"

> "TypeScript: 1/3 to 1/2 of diffs are type wrestling."

### On Agents

> "That's you, Human. As the Overseer, you have an identity in the system, and your own inbox, and you can send and receive town mail."

> "Build a colony of coding agents, not the world's largest ant."

---

## 12. Comparison with Other Patterns

### Gas Town vs Ralph Wiggum

| Aspect | Ralph Wiggum | Gas Town |
|--------|--------------|----------|
| **Model** | Single agent, retry loop | Multi-agent factory |
| **Complexity** | Bash script | Full system |
| **Persistence** | Via git/progress.txt | Beads data plane |
| **Parallelism** | None (sequential) | Native (many agents) |
| **Roles** | None | 8 specialized roles |
| **Setup** | Minutes | Hours/days |
| **Cost** | Single agent | Multiple accounts |
| **Use Case** | Well-defined features | Complex systems, ongoing dev |

**When to use Ralph:** Single feature, clear completion criteria, budget-conscious
**When to use Gas Town:** Building entire products, team-scale output needed

---

### Gas Town vs CC Mirror

| Aspect | CC Mirror | Gas Town |
|--------|-----------|----------|
| **Model** | Task-based DAG | Agent factory |
| **Complexity** | Medium | High |
| **Setup** | npx command | Go install + config |
| **Dependencies** | TaskCreate/BlockedBy | Beads + Agent Mail |
| **Parallelism** | Auto-scheduled | Explicit workers |
| **Roles** | None (generic agents) | 8 specialized |
| **Persistence** | Built-in tasks | Git via Beads |
| **Cost** | Single variant | Multiple accounts |

**nummanali's take:**
> "Simplicity covers 80% with zero effort - mass-market ease. Gas Town for remaining 20%."

**When to use CC Mirror:** Most projects, getting started with multi-agent
**When to use Gas Town:** Stage 7+ scale, maximum throughput

---

### Gas Town vs Infinite Orchestra

| Aspect | Orchestra | Gas Town |
|--------|-----------|----------|
| **Model** | Self-improving | Production factory |
| **Environment** | Docker container | tmux + local |
| **Autonomy** | High (improves itself) | Human-directed |
| **Parallelism** | Sequential (for now) | Native parallel |
| **Roles** | Profiles (coder, arch) | 8 fixed roles |
| **Persistence** | Neo4j optional | Beads |
| **24/7** | Yes (designed for) | Yes (tmux) |

**When to use Orchestra:** Experimental, self-evolving systems
**When to use Gas Town:** Production development, human oversight

---

### Pattern Comparison Summary

```
‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
‚îÇ                    ORCHESTRATOR SPECTRUM                         ‚îÇ
```

- [Revenge of the Junior Developer](https://sourcegraph.com/blog/revenge-of-the-junior-developer) - Wave framework
- [The Brute Squad](https://sourcegraph.com/blog/the-brute-squad) - Multi-agent philosophy

#### GitHub Repositories
- [steveyegge/gastown](https://github.com/steveyegge/gastown) - Multi-agent workspace manager
- [steveyegge/beads](https://github.com/steveyegge/beads) - Agent memory system (~225K lines Go)
- [steveyegge/mcp_agent_mail](https://github.com/steveyegge/mcp_agent_mail) - Inter-agent communication
- [steveyegge/vc](https://github.com/steveyegge/vc) - AI-orchestrated coding agent colony
- [steveyegge/efrit](https://github.com/steveyegge/efrit) - Native elisp coding agent for Emacs

```bash
/plugin marketplace add numman-ali/n-skills
/plugin install gastown@numman-ali/n-skills
```

## Appendix: Quick Reference

### Installation Commands

```bash
# Install
go install github.com/steveyegge/gastown/cmd/gt@latest

# Initialize
gt init
gt rig add /path/to/repo
```

### Role Management

```bash
# Town-level
gt mayor up|down|status
gt deacon up|down|status
gt dogs up|down|status|bark

# Rig-level
gt witness up|down <rig>
gt refinery up|down <rig>
gt polecat up|down|list <rig> [name]
gt crew spawn|count|purge <rig>
```

### Inbox

```bash
gt inbox                     # View pending
gt inbox respond <id> --approve|--reject
gt inbox clear
```

### Town Management

```bash
gt status                    # Town-wide status
gt town down                 # Stop all agents
gt town reset --soft|--hard  # Reset state
gt config set|get|list       # Configuration
```

### Beads

```bash
gt beads sync --force
gt beads reset
bd ready
bd create "Task title"
bd dep add <child> <parent>
```

---

## Cost Estimation

```
Role-based cost per hour (estimates):
‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ
Mayor (Opus):      $15-20/hour
Refinery (Opus):   $15-20/hour
Dogs (Sonnet):     $5-8/hour
Polecats (Sonnet): $5-10/hour each
Witness (Haiku):   $1-3/hour
Deacon (Haiku):    $1-2/hour
Crew (Haiku):      $0.50-2/hour each

Example daily cost:
‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ‚îÅ
1 Mayor + 1 Deacon + 1 Dogs + 2 Rigs + 3 Polecats + 5 Crew
= $18 + $1.5 + $7 + $40 + $22.5 + $5
= ~$94/hour (rough estimate)

8 hours = ~$752/day (heavy usage)
Conservative usage = $50-100/day
```

```html
    }

      border: 1px solid var(--color-border);
    }


    /* ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
       SKIP LINK ‚Äî Accessibility

      }

    /* ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

          <h2>1. Who is Steve Yegge?</h2>

          <h3>Professional Background</h3>

          <p>Steve Yegge is a 40-year software development veteran with a career that provides unique credibility for building Gas Town:</p>

          <!-- Mechanism #18: Data Table ‚Äî compact authority through structured facts -->
          <table class="data-table">
            <thead>
              <tr>
                <th>Company</th>
                <th>Role</th>
                <th>Relevance</th>
              </tr>
            </thead>
            <tbody>
              <tr>
                <td><strong>Amazon</strong></td>
                <td>Early employee</td>
                <td>Built internal tools at scale</td>
              </tr>
              <tr>
                <td><strong>Google</strong></td>
                <td>Senior Engineer</td>
                <td>Famous for "Stevey's Blog Rants," internal platforms</td>
              </tr>
              <tr>
                <td><strong>Sourcegraph</strong></td>
                <td>Senior role</td>
                <td>Code intelligence, developer tooling</td>
              </tr>
              <tr>
                <td><strong>Current</strong></td>
                <td>Full-time AI development advocate</td>
                <td>Building the future of agent-assisted dev</td>
              </tr>
            </tbody>
          </table>

          <h3>Why His Opinion Matters</h3>

          <ul>
            <li><strong>~1 million lines vibe-coded in 2025</strong> ‚Äî Not theory, practice</li>
            <li><strong>Built Beads (225K lines of Go)</strong> ‚Äî Proof of concept at scale</li>
            <li><strong>Built Gas Town using Gas Town</strong> ‚Äî Recursive validation</li>
            <li><strong>Transparent about limitations</strong> ‚Äî Warns about chaos, costs, maturity</li>
            <li><strong>Decades of platform engineering</strong> ‚Äî Knows what scales and what breaks</li>
          </ul>

          <h3>Public Presence</h3>

          <ul class="presence-list">
            <li><strong>Twitter/X:</strong> @steve_yegge (primary announcements)</li>
            <li><strong>Medium:</strong> steve-yegge.medium.com (deep philosophical pieces)</li>
            <li><strong>GitHub:</strong> github.com/steveyegge (Gas Town, Beads, MCP Agent Mail)</li>
            <li><strong>Podcasts:</strong> Changelog, O'Reilly Radar</li>
          </ul>

          <h3>The "Vibe Coding" Pioneer</h3>

          <p>Steve didn't just adopt AI-assisted development ‚Äî he pioneered "vibe coding" as a philosophy:</p>

          <!-- Key quote ‚Äî Instrument Serif italic, generous margins
               This quote establishes Yegge's voice before the paradigm crack -->
          <blockquote class="key-quote">
            <p>"Work becomes fluid, an uncountable that you sling around freely, like slopping shiny fish into wooden barrels at the docks."</p>
          </blockquote>

          <h4>Vibe coding principles:</h4>

          <ul class="vibe-principles">
            <li>Describe what you want (the "vibe")</li>
            <li>AI generates the code</li>
            <li>You never read the code directly</li>
            <li>Judge by outcomes, not implementation</li>
            <li>Accept some bugs, focus on throughput</li>
          </ul>

        </section>


      </div>
    </div>

          <h3>The Factory Metaphor</h3>

          <p>Gas Town isn't an agent ‚Äî it's a <strong>factory for agents</strong>:</p>

          <!-- Comparison table: old role vs new role
               Mechanism #18: Data Table with Gas Town column emphasized -->
          <table class="factory-table">

              <tr>

              </tr>

                <td>You write code</td>
                <td>You file features</td>
              </tr>
              <tr>
                <td>You debug</td>
                <td>Agents debug</td>
              </tr>
              <tr>
                <td>You're the implementer</td>
                <td>You're the PM</td>
              </tr>
              <tr>
                <td>Single context window</td>
                <td>Many workers, shared memory</td>
              </tr>
              <tr>

                <td>Workers persist, memory survives</td>
              </tr>
            </tbody>
          </table>

          <!-- Second major quote ‚Äî slightly less dramatic than paradigm-crack
               but still Instrument Serif, generous margins -->

          <p>You're not writing code anymore. You're managing a factory.</p>


          <h3>Why "Gas Town"?</h3>

          <p>The Mad Max: Fury Road reference isn't accidental:</p>

          <ul class="why-list">
            <li><strong>Post-apocalyptic resourcefulness</strong> <span>‚Äî Work with chaos, not against it</span></li>
            <li><strong>Clear role hierarchy</strong> <span>‚Äî Mayor, Deacon, Dogs, Workers</span></li>
            <li><strong>Survival-focused</strong> <span>‚Äî Throughput over perfection</span></li>
            <li><strong>Community-built</strong> <span>‚Äî Everyone contributes to the economy</span></li>
          </ul>

        </section>

          <div class="section-meta">Operations Stratum ¬∑ Architecture</div>
          <h2>3. The 8 Roles Architecture</h2>

          <p>Gas Town runs on 8 named roles organized into three tiers. Each role has a specific function, a recommended model tier, and a set of CLI commands. This is the full machine ‚Äî the factory floor revealed.</p>

          <!-- R5: Info callout opens the section ‚Äî orientation before density peak
               S3: first component sets tone = "helpful guide"
               Mechanism #10: blue border-left signals informational -->
          <div class="callout callout--info" role="note">
            <div class="callout-label">Info</div>
            <div class="callout-body">
              <p>Town-level roles run once per Gas Town instance (global coordination). Rig-level roles run per-project ‚Äî you can have multiple rigs. The Overseer is you: the human boss who manages through an inbox, not through code.</p>
            </div>
          </div>


          <!-- ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

                <div class="role-card-header">
                  <span class="role-card-name">2. Deacon</span>
                  <span class="model-badge model-badge--haiku">Haiku</span>
                </div>
                <div class="role-card-function">Health monitoring and agent coordination</div>
                <div class="role-card-body">
                  <h4>Responsibilities</h4>
                  <ul>
                    <li>Monitors agent health across the town</li>
                    <li>Handles agent-to-agent handshakes</li>
                    <li>Reports anomalies to Mayor</li>
                    <li>Tracks work progress</li>
                    <li>Manages handoff protocols and worker recycling</li>
                  </ul>
                  <h4>Commands</h4>
                  <div class="role-commands"><code><span class="fn">gt</span> <span class="str">deacon</span> <span class="str">up</span>       <span class="cmt"># Start deacon</span>
<span class="fn">gt</span> <span class="str">deacon</span> <span class="str">status</span>   <span class="cmt"># View monitoring state</span></code></div>
                </div>
              </div>

              <!-- 3. DOGS ‚Äî Quality gates
                   Sonnet-level: reasoning but not Opus-level
                   Mechanism #9: blue badge = moderate capability -->
              <div class="role-card">
                <div class="role-card-header">
                  <span class="role-card-name">3. Dogs</span>
                  <span class="model-badge model-badge--sonnet">Sonnet</span>
                </div>
                <div class="role-card-function">Quality assurance and safety gates ‚Äî town-level grunts</div>
                <div class="role-card-body">
                  <h4>Responsibilities</h4>
                  <ul>
                    <li>Reviews work before acceptance</li>
                    <li>Enforces quality standards</li>
                    <li>Guards against regressions</li>
                    <li>Can reject/rollback work</li>
                    <li>Stale branch cleanup</li>
                  </ul>
                  <h4>Commands</h4>
                  <div class="role-commands"><code><span class="fn">gt</span> <span class="str">dogs</span> <span class="str">up</span>         <span class="cmt"># Start dogs</span>
<span class="fn">gt</span> <span class="str">dogs</span> <span class="str">bark</span>       <span class="cmt"># Trigger quality check</span></code></div>
                </div>
              </div>

            </div>
          </div>


          <!-- R5: spacing shift between role clusters prevents information fatigue
               R3: density debt payment ‚Äî 3 dense cards demand a breathing line
               Type 2 transition: same domain (roles), different intensity (tier shift) -->
          <hr class="section-divider" aria-hidden="true">


          <!-- ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
               RIG-LEVEL ROLES: Refinery, Polecat, Witness, Crew
               The workers. Refinery and Polecat get larger treatment
               (architecturally critical). Witness and Crew are compact.
               R5: vary density between roles ‚Äî not identical cards
               ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ -->
          <div class="role-cluster">
            <div class="role-cluster-label">Rig-Level Roles ‚Äî Per-Project Workers</div>

            <!-- Refinery + Polecat: the two major rig roles
                 2-column grid ‚Äî both are architecturally critical
                 Featured treatment: darker borders, Opus/Sonnet badges -->
            <div class="role-grid role-grid--two">

              <!-- 4. REFINERY ‚Äî Task decomposition
                   Featured role: Opus-level reasoning for architectural decomposition
                   Mechanism #1: dark border signals architectural weight -->
              <div class="role-card role-card--featured">
                <div class="role-card-header">
                  <span class="role-card-name">4. Refinery</span>
                  <span class="model-badge model-badge--opus">Opus 4.5</span>
                </div>
                <div class="role-card-function">Breaks down large tasks into agent-sized work</div>
                <div class="role-card-body">
                  <h4>Responsibilities</h4>
                  <ul>
                    <li>Receives feature requests from Mayor</li>
                    <li>Decomposes into smaller, atomic tasks</li>
                    <li>Assigns to Polecats or Crew</li>
                    <li>Tracks decomposition progress</li>
                    <li>Manages the merge queue with sequential rebasing</li>
                  </ul>
                  <h4>Commands</h4>
                  <div class="role-commands"><code><span class="fn">gt</span> <span class="str">refinery</span> <span class="str">up</span> <span class="typ">&lt;rig&gt;</span>           <span class="cmt"># Start refinery for rig</span>
<span class="fn">gt</span> <span class="str">refinery</span> <span class="str">decompose</span> <span class="typ">&lt;task&gt;</span>   <span class="cmt"># Manually trigger decomposition</span></code></div>
                </div>
              </div>

              <!-- 5. POLECAT ‚Äî Named persistent workers
                   Featured: the main workhorse (Sonnet-level)
                   Mechanism #1: dark border ‚Äî this is where work happens -->
              <div class="role-card role-card--featured">
                <div class="role-card-header">
                  <span class="role-card-name">5. Polecat</span>
                  <span class="model-badge model-badge--sonnet">Sonnet</span>
                </div>
                <div class="role-card-function">Named, persistent agent workers with specializations</div>
                <div class="role-card-body">
                  <h4>Responsibilities</h4>
                  <ul>
                    <li>Execute assigned tasks</li>
                    <li>Maintain context across sessions</li>
                    <li>Specialize in rig-specific knowledge</li>
                    <li>Report completion to Refinery</li>
                    <li>Ephemeral but can be persistent workspaces</li>
                  </ul>
                  <h4>Commands</h4>
                  <div class="role-commands"><code><span class="fn">gt</span> <span class="str">polecat</span> <span class="str">up</span> <span class="typ">&lt;rig&gt;</span> <span class="str">alice</span>      <span class="cmt"># Start polecat named "alice"</span>
<span class="fn">gt</span> <span class="str">polecat</span> <span class="str">up</span> <span class="typ">&lt;rig&gt;</span> <span class="str">bob</span>        <span class="cmt"># Start polecat named "bob"</span>
<span class="fn">gt</span> <span class="str">polecat</span> <span class="str">list</span> <span class="typ">&lt;rig&gt;</span>          <span class="cmt"># List polecats for rig</span>
<span class="fn">gt</span> <span class="str">polecat</span> <span class="str">assign</span> <span class="str">alice</span> <span class="typ">&lt;task&gt;</span> <span class="cmt"># Assign task to alice</span></code></div>
                  <div class="naming-note">Naming convention: Human names (alice, bob, carol) help with mental model</div>
                </div>
              </div>

            </div>

            <!-- Witness + Crew: supporting rig roles
                 2-column grid, more compact ‚Äî lighter border treatment
                 R5: density variation ‚Äî these are less architecturally heavy -->
            <div class="role-grid role-grid--two" style="margin-top: var(--space-6);">

              <!-- 6. WITNESS ‚Äî Per-rig observer
                   Haiku-level: observation and logging
                   Standard treatment: lighter border = supporting role -->
              <div class="role-card">
                <div class="role-card-header">
                  <span class="role-card-name">6. Witness</span>
                  <span class="model-badge model-badge--haiku">Haiku</span>
                </div>
                <div class="role-card-function">Observes and records rig activity ‚Äî watches over polecats</div>
                <div class="role-card-body">
                  <h4>Responsibilities</h4>
                  <ul>
                    <li>Watches all work in assigned rig</li>
                    <li>Records history and context</li>
                    <li>Provides state to new workers</li>
                    <li>Reports anomalies to Deacon</li>
                    <li>Unsticks drifting agents</li>
                  </ul>
                  <h4>Commands</h4>
                  <div class="role-commands"><code><span class="fn">gt</span> <span class="str">witness</span> <span class="str">up</span> <span class="typ">&lt;rig&gt;</span>    <span class="cmt"># Start witness for rig</span>
<span class="fn">gt</span> <span class="str">witness</span> <span class="str">report</span>      <span class="cmt"># Get current state report</span></code></div>
                </div>
              </div>

              <!-- 7. CREW ‚Äî Ephemeral burst workers
                   Haiku-level: simple isolated tasks
                   Standard treatment: disposable = lightest border weight -->
              <div class="role-card">
                <div class="role-card-header">
                  <span class="role-card-name">7. Crew</span>
                  <span class="model-badge model-badge--haiku">Haiku</span>
                </div>
                <div class="role-card-function">Short-lived, task-specific burst workers</div>
                <div class="role-card-body">
                  <h4>Responsibilities</h4>
                  <ul>
                    <li>Execute single tasks</li>
                    <li>No persistent state</li>
                    <li>Cheap and disposable</li>
                    <li>Used for parallel bursts</li>
                    <li>Spawn, complete, disappear</li>
                  </ul>
                  <h4>Commands</h4>
                  <div class="role-commands"><code><span class="fn">gt</span> <span class="str">crew</span> <span class="str">spawn</span> <span class="typ">&lt;rig&gt;</span> <span class="str">--task</span> <span class="str">"fix this bug"</span>
<span class="fn">gt</span> <span class="str">crew</span> <span class="str">count</span> <span class="typ">&lt;rig&gt;</span>    <span class="cmt"># Count active crew</span>
<span class="fn">gt</span> <span class="str">crew</span> <span class="str">purge</span> <span class="typ">&lt;rig&gt;</span>    <span class="cmt"># Kill all crew</span></code></div>
                </div>
              </div>

            </div>
          </div>


          <!-- R5: spacing shift before human level
               The Overseer is set apart ‚Äî you, the human, are separate from the machine -->
          <hr class="section-divider" aria-hidden="true">


          <!-- ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
               HUMAN-LEVEL ROLE: Overseer (YOU)
               Full-width, inverted header. The reader IS this role.
               R5: temperature shift ‚Äî warm (you are welcomed here)
               Mechanism #13: dark header echoed at card level
               ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ -->
          <div class="role-cluster">
            <div class="role-cluster-label">Human Level ‚Äî You</div>

            <div class="role-grid role-grid--one">

              <!-- 8. OVERSEER ‚Äî Product Manager (the reader)
                   Inverted header mirrors the page header ‚Äî you are the shell
                   Mechanism #1: 4px border = highest importance
                   Mechanism #13: dark header at component level = structural echo -->
              <div class="role-card role-card--featured role-card--overseer" style="border-width: var(--border-accent);">
                <div class="role-card-header">
                  <span class="role-card-name">8. Overseer (YOU)</span>
                </div>
                <div class="role-card-function">Product Manager and decision maker</div>
                <div class="role-card-body">
                  <h4>Responsibilities</h4>
                  <ul>
                    <li>Define features and priorities</li>
                    <li>Review inbox decisions</li>
                    <li>Approve major changes</li>
                    <li>Provide human judgment</li>
                    <li>Has identity in the system with own inbox</li>
                  </ul>
                  <h4>Interface</h4>
                  <ul>
                    <li>Human inbox for decisions</li>
                    <li>tmux panes for observation</li>
                    <li><code>gt</code> CLI for commands</li>
                    <li>Can send and receive town mail</li>
                  </ul>
                </div>
              </div>

            </div>

            <!-- Yegge's voice on the Overseer role
                 Instrument Serif italic ‚Äî the voice of the architect explaining YOUR place
                 R5: key-quote after heavy component = decompression -->
            <blockquote class="key-quote" style="margin-top: var(--space-6);">
              <p>"That's you, Human. As the Overseer, you have an identity in the system, and your own inbox, and you can send and receive town mail."</p>
            </blockquote>
          </div>


          <!-- R5: Tip callout ‚Äî fast component after slow sequence = velocity relief
               R3: density debt payment after 8 dense role cards
               Practical, warm, grounding ‚Äî brings the reader back from awe -->
          <div class="callout callout--tip" role="note">
            <div class="callout-label">Tip</div>
            <div class="callout-body">
              <p>Model recommendations are about cost optimization, not capability gates. You <em>can</em> run all roles on Opus 4.5 ‚Äî but Haiku handles observation and simple tasks at a fraction of the cost. Save your Opus budget for the coordinators (Mayor) and decomposers (Refinery) where complex reasoning actually matters.</p>
            </div>
          </div>


          <!-- ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
               COMMUNICATION FLOW ‚Äî The machine running
               Shows how a feature request flows through all 8 roles.
               This resolves the roles into action ‚Äî not just sitting.
               R3: density MEDIUM after the HIGH peak of role deep dives
               R4: F-pattern ‚Äî left-aligned role names, scanning down
               Mechanism #18: structured data flow (table-like)
               ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê -->
          <h3>Role Communication Flow</h3>

          <p>A feature request enters the system and flows through the roles. This is the machine running ‚Äî not just its parts on display, but the parts in motion:</p>

          <div class="comm-flow" role="figure" aria-label="Communication flow showing how a feature request moves through Gas Town roles from Overseer to completion">
            <div class="comm-flow-title">Feature Request Flow: "Build user authentication"</div>
            <div class="comm-flow-body">

              <div class="flow-step">
                <div class="flow-role flow-role--primary">Overseer</div>
                <div class="flow-action"><strong>"Build user authentication"</strong> ‚Äî filed as feature request</div>
              </div>
              <div class="flow-connector"><div class="flow-arrow"></div></div>

              <div class="flow-step">
                <div class="flow-role">Mayor</div>
                <div class="flow-action"><strong>Routes to rig</strong> ‚Äî selects appropriate project, sends status reports back</div>
              </div>
              <div class="flow-connector"><div class="flow-arrow"></div></div>

              <div class="flow-step">
                <div class="flow-role">Refinery</div>
                <div class="flow-action"><strong>Decomposes into tasks:</strong></div>
              </div>
              <div class="flow-branch">
                <span>‚Äî task 1: DB schema</span>
                <span>‚Äî task 2: API routes</span>
                <span>‚Äî task 3: Frontend forms</span>
              </div>
              <div class="flow-connector"><div class="flow-arrow"></div></div>

              <div class="flow-step">
                <div class="flow-role">Polecat: alice</div>
                <div class="flow-action"><strong>Executes task 1</strong> ‚Äî observed by Witness throughout</div>
              </div>

              <div class="flow-step">
                <div class="flow-role">Polecat: bob</div>
                <div class="flow-action"><strong>Executes task 2</strong> ‚Äî in parallel</div>
              </div>

              <div class="flow-step">
                <div class="flow-role">Crew: temp-1</div>
                <div class="flow-action"><strong>Executes task 3</strong> ‚Äî ephemeral burst worker</div>
              </div>
              <div class="flow-connector"><div class="flow-arrow"></div></div>

              <div class="flow-step">
                <div class="flow-role">Witness</div>
                <div class="flow-action"><strong>Observes all activity</strong> ‚Äî on anomaly, reports to Deacon</div>
              </div>
              <div class="flow-connector"><div class="flow-arrow"></div></div>

              <div class="flow-step">
                <div class="flow-role">Dogs</div>
                <div class="flow-action"><strong>Quality check</strong> ‚Äî reviews work, enforces standards, can reject/rollback</div>
              </div>
              <div class="flow-connector"><div class="flow-arrow"></div></div>

              <div class="flow-step">
                <div class="flow-role flow-role--primary">Complete</div>
                <div class="flow-action"><strong>Work passes gates</strong> ‚Äî merged, delivered, done</div>
              </div>

            </div>
          </div>


          <!-- R5: Gotcha callout ‚Äî protective warning before section close
               The merge queue detail is critical: parallel execution, serial integration
               This is where "chaos against architecture" lives concretely
               R5: S4 resolution ‚Äî don't end on anxiety, end on understanding -->
          <div class="callout callout--gotcha" role="note">
            <div class="callout-label">Gotcha</div>
            <div class="callout-body">
              <p>The merge queue is <strong>sequential, not parallel</strong>. While Polecats and Crew execute tasks in parallel, merging happens one branch at a time through sequential rebasing. This is the architecture managing chaos ‚Äî parallel execution, serial integration.</p>
            </div>
          </div>

          <!-- R5: Challenge callout ‚Äî closing invitation after understanding the machine
               R5: S4 resolution ‚Äî end on invitation, not anxiety
               R5: temperature = warm (inviting) after cold (gotcha) = natural arc -->
          <div class="callout callout--challenge" role="note">
            <div class="callout-label">Challenge</div>
            <div class="callout-body">
              <p>Trace a real feature you've built recently through the 8-role flow above. Where would the decomposition happen? Which tasks would be Polecat-persistent vs Crew-ephemeral? If you can map your own work onto this architecture, you're ready for the next section.</p>
            </div>
          </div>

        </section>


      </div>
    </div>


    <!-- ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
         INFRASTRUCTURE STRATUM ‚Äî Pipe
         The hidden plumbing below the factory floor.
         Beads: the memory system that prevents agent amnesia.
         Arc: After the operational peak, the reader descends into systems.
         "Oh, THAT's how they share memory."
         Density: MEDIUM-HIGH, more narrative than roles section.
         R3: geological model ‚Üí descending into infrastructure
         Transition: HARD CUT from Operations (domain change: roles ‚Üí memory)
         ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê -->
    <div class="stratum stratum--pipe stratum-boundary--hard">
      <div class="page-spine">


        <section id="beads-the-memory-system" class="section" aria-label="Beads: The Memory System">
          <div class="section-meta">Infrastructure Stratum ¬∑ Memory System</div>
          <h2>Beads: The Memory System</h2>


          <!-- "50 First Dates" ‚Äî The opening quote grounds emotionally
               After 8 dense role cards, this is immediately relatable and human.
               R5: essence callout ‚Üí slow, contemplative ‚Üí density relief after peak
               Instrument Serif italic for the deepest voice -->
          <h3>The "50 First Dates" Problem</h3>

          <blockquote class="paradigm-quote" style="margin-top: var(--space-4);">
            <p>"Agents suffer from '50 First Dates' syndrome ‚Äî they wake up with no memory of yesterday."</p>
          </blockquote>

          <p>Every new Claude session starts fresh. This is the fundamental problem Beads solves.</p>


          <!-- R5: spacing shift within same domain (overview ‚Üí detail) -->
          <hr class="section-divider" aria-hidden="true">


          <!-- Why Markdown Plans Fail ‚Äî The failure modes
               Data table showing concrete problems.
               R5: decision matrix variant ‚Äî problem/consequence pairs
               Mechanism #18: Data table with structural headers -->
          <h3>Why Markdown Plans Fail at Scale</h3>

          <table class="data-table" role="table">
            <thead>
              <tr>
                <th>Problem</th>
                <th>Consequence</th>
              </tr>
            </thead>
            <tbody>
              <tr>
                <td class="fail-table">Not queryable</td>
                <td>Agents must parse dozens of files to reconstruct work graph</td>
              </tr>
              <tr>
                <td class="fail-table">No dependency tracking</td>
                <td>Agents can't compute which tasks are unblocked</td>
              </tr>
              <tr>
                <td class="fail-table">Conflict-prone</td>
                <td>Multiple agents editing same files</td>
              </tr>
              <tr>
                <td class="fail-table">Implicit task stacks</td>
                <td>"Intelligent wandering" without clear direction</td>
              </tr>
            </tbody>
          </table>


          <!-- R5: spacing shift ‚Äî failure modes ‚Üí solution -->
          <hr class="section-divider" aria-hidden="true">


          <!-- What Beads Does ‚Äî The solution description
               Features in 2-column grid for density without clutter
               R5: info callout ‚Üí context before structure
               Mechanism #15: Bento-like grid for feature catalog -->
          <h3>What Beads Does</h3>

          <p><strong>Beads</strong> (<code>github.com/steveyegge/beads</code>) is a ~225K line Go project providing:</p>

          <div class="features-grid">
            <div class="feature-item"><strong>Git-backed storage:</strong> All state persisted in git</div>
            <div class="feature-item"><strong>Universal context:</strong> Shared context across all agents</div>
            <div class="feature-item"><strong>Memory management:</strong> Agents can read/write context</div>
            <div class="feature-item"><strong>Hash-based IDs:</strong> (e.g., <code>bd-a1b2</code>) prevent merge conflicts</div>
            <div class="feature-item"><strong>Dependency tracking:</strong> Explicit links between tasks</div>
            <div class="feature-item"><strong>Memory decay:</strong> Compaction summarizes old closed tasks</div>
          </div>


          <!-- R5: spacing shift ‚Äî features ‚Üí architecture -->
          <hr class="section-divider" aria-hidden="true">


          <!-- Beads Architecture ‚Äî The plumbing diagram
               Reuses role-hierarchy pattern for structural consistency
               Dark title bar echoes refinery header shell
               Mechanism #13: Dark header at component level
               R4: hub-and-spoke ‚Äî Beads data plane is the hub -->
          <h3>Beads Architecture</h3>

          <div class="role-hierarchy" role="figure" aria-label="Beads architecture showing Gas Town roles connecting through the Beads data plane to Git repository">
            <div class="role-hierarchy-title">Beads Architecture</div>

            <div class="hierarchy-tier">
              <div class="tier-label tier-label--town">Gas Town Roles</div>
              <div class="tier-boxes">
                <div class="role-box">
                  <div class="role-box-name">Mayor</div>
                </div>
                <div class="role-box">
                  <div class="role-box-name">Polecat</div>
                </div>
                <div class="role-box">
                  <div class="role-box-name">Crew</div>
                </div>
              </div>
            </div>

            <div class="tier-connector"><div class="tier-connector-line"></div></div>

            <div class="hierarchy-tier">
              <div class="tier-label">Data Plane</div>
              <div class="tier-boxes tier-boxes--single">
                <div class="role-box" style="border-color: var(--color-text); border-width: var(--border-accent);">
                  <div class="role-box-name">BEADS</div>
                  <div class="role-box-desc">Data Plane</div>
                </div>
              </div>
            </div>

            <div class="tier-connector"><div class="tier-connector-line"></div></div>

            <div class="hierarchy-tier">
              <div class="tier-label">Persistence</div>
              <div class="tier-boxes tier-boxes--single">
                <div class="role-box">
                  <div class="role-box-name">Git Repository</div>
                </div>
              </div>
            </div>
          </div>


          <!-- R5: spacing shift ‚Äî architecture ‚Üí commands -->
          <hr class="section-divider" aria-hidden="true">


          <!-- Key Beads Commands ‚Äî The hands-on interface
               Dark code block for CLI precision
               Mechanism #17: Code block (dark background + syntax)
               R5: code snippet velocity = SLOW, needs breathing before and after -->
          <h3>Key Beads Commands</h3>

          <div class="code-block"><code><span class="fn">bd</span> <span class="str">ready</span>           <span class="cmt"># List tasks with zero blockers (what can be done NOW)</span>
<span class="fn">bd</span> <span class="str">create</span> <span class="str">"Title"</span>  <span class="cmt"># Create new task</span>
<span class="fn">bd</span> <span class="str">dep</span> <span class="str">add</span> <span class="typ">X</span> <span class="typ">Y</span>     <span class="cmt"># X is blocked by Y</span>
<span class="fn">bd</span> <span class="str">show</span> <span class="typ">&lt;id&gt;</span>       <span class="cmt"># Full task state and history</span></code></div>


          <!-- R5: spacing shift ‚Äî commands ‚Üí memory model -->
          <hr class="section-divider" aria-hidden="true">


          <!-- Memory Model ‚Äî The 3-layer retrieval hierarchy
               Hot/Warm/Cold with border-weight gradient encoding priority
               This is the section's structural peak ‚Äî the hidden plumbing revealed
               Mechanism #1: Border-weight gradient (4px/3px/1px)
               Mechanism #7: Zone differentiation within layers
               R3: geological model ‚Üí strata within strata -->
          <h3>Memory Model</h3>

          <div class="memory-model" role="figure" aria-label="Beads memory model showing three layers: hot context, warm context, and cold context with retrieval priority">
            <div class="memory-model-title">Beads Memory Model</div>

            <div class="memory-layer memory-layer--hot">
              <div class="memory-layer-label">Layer 1: Hot Context (RAM-cached)</div>
              <ul>
                <li>Current task state</li>
                <li>Last N interactions</li>
                <li>Active file references</li>
              </ul>
            </div>

            <div class="memory-layer memory-layer--warm">
              <div class="memory-layer-label">Layer 2: Warm Context (SQLite + Git index)</div>
              <ul>
                <li>Recent commit history</li>
                <li>Cross-agent message log</li>
                <li>Rig state snapshots</li>
              </ul>
            </div>

            <div class="memory-layer memory-layer--cold">
              <div class="memory-layer-label">Layer 3: Cold Context (Git history)</div>
              <ul>
                <li>Full project history</li>
                <li>Previous run outcomes</li>
                <li>Archived decisions</li>
              </ul>
            </div>

            <div class="memory-retrieval">Retrieval: Hot ‚Üí Warm ‚Üí Cold (only query cold if needed)</div>
          </div>


          <!-- R5: spacing shift ‚Äî memory model ‚Üí git rationale -->
          <hr class="section-divider" aria-hidden="true">


          <!-- Why Git as Database ‚Äî The closing principle
               Essence callout + concrete reasons
               R5: S4 resolution pattern ‚Äî end on understanding, not anxiety
               R5: teaching moment sequence: Essence (principle) ‚Üí list (practical) -->
          <h3>Why Git as Database?</h3>

          <!-- R5: essence callout ‚Äî the principle behind the choice
               Instrument Serif italic for the deepest voice -->
          <div class="callout callout--essence" role="note">
            <div class="callout-label">Essence</div>
            <div class="callout-body">
              <p>"Git as database provides durable, diffable, auditable storage with zero infrastructure."</p>
            </div>
          </div>

          <ul class="git-reasons">
            <li><strong>Survives crashes:</strong> Everything is committed</li>
            <li><strong>Audit trail:</strong> Full history of all agent actions</li>
            <li><strong>Recovery:</strong> Roll back to any point in time</li>
            <li><strong>Sharing:</strong> Multiple agents share the same store</li>
            <li><strong>No heavyweight message bus required</strong></li>
          </ul>

          <!-- R5: tip callout ‚Äî warm, practical, grounding after infrastructure density
               R5: S4 resolution ‚Üí end section with practical wisdom, not complexity -->
          <div class="callout callout--tip" role="note">
            <div class="callout-label">Tip</div>
            <div class="callout-body">
              <p>Beads' hash-based IDs (<code>bd-a1b2</code>) are the key insight: because no two agents ever generate the same task ID, merge conflicts become structurally impossible. This is what makes parallel agents viable ‚Äî the data model itself prevents collision.</p>
            </div>
          </div>

        </section>


      </div>
    </div>


    <!-- ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

         ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê -->

             ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê -->
        <section id="the-6-waves-of-ai" class="section" aria-label="The 6 Waves of AI">
          <div class="section-meta">Principles Stratum ¬∑ Historical Context</div>
          <h2>The 6 Waves of AI</h2>

          <p>Steve frames the evolution of AI-assisted development as six overlapping waves:</p>

          <!-- R5: data table ‚Äî the historical sweep
               Mechanism #18: Data table with mono headers
               Wave 6 highlighted as current ‚Äî the reader's temporal position
               Mechanism #9: Color encoding on target row -->
          <table class="data-table" role="table">
            <thead>
              <tr>
                <th>Wave</th>
                <th>Era</th>
                <th>Description</th>
                <th>Productivity</th>
              </tr>
            </thead>
            <tbody>
              <tr>
                <td>1</td>
                <td>Pre-2022</td>
                <td>Traditional manual coding</td>
                <td>Baseline</td>
              </tr>
              <tr>
                <td>2</td>
                <td>2023</td>
                <td>Completions-based (Copilot-style)</td>
                <td>~2x</td>
              </tr>
              <tr>
                <td>3</td>
                <td>2024</td>
                <td>Chat-based (CHOP)</td>
                <td>~5x</td>
              </tr>
              <tr>
                <td>4</td>
                <td>2025 H1</td>
                <td>Coding agents (Claude Code, Amp, Codex)</td>
                <td>~10x</td>
              </tr>
              <tr>
                <td>5</td>
                <td>2025 H2</td>
                <td>Agent clusters (multi-agent parallel)</td>
                <td>~25x</td>
              </tr>
              <tr class="wave-current">
                <td><strong>6</strong></td>
                <td><strong>2026+</strong></td>
                <td><strong>Agent fleets (AI supervisors managing swarms)</strong></td>
                <td><strong>~50x+</strong></td>
              </tr>
            </tbody>
          </table>

          <p><strong>Gas Town is Wave 6 infrastructure.</strong></p>


          <!-- R5: spacing shift ‚Äî waves ‚Üí stages (same domain, different granularity) -->
          <hr class="section-divider" aria-hidden="true">


          <!-- 8 Stages of Dev Evolution ‚Äî Individual developer progression

        <!-- ‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
```
